✻ Brewed for 1m 10s
❯ in js I do this:   const { responder_Discovery, MsgEnv } =                    
  ref_IPSME_Bridge.current;                                                     
  don't suppose that is possible in c++?                                        
  I mean get the return of multiple variables instead of having to get each     
  variable individually                                                         

● Yes — C++ has this, it's called structured bindings (C++17, and you're already
  on /std:c++20). The catch vs JS: it's positional, not by-name. You can't
  reach into an arbitrary object and pluck members by name — the object has to
  be a tuple, a pair, or a struct with public members, and the binding matches
  by declaration order, not by the names you write.

  So IPSME_Bridge (private members + accessors) can't be destructured directly.
  You expose a bundle, then bind it:

  Option A — a small named struct (my recommendation, most readable):
  // in IPSME_Bridge
  struct Refs {
      Responder_Discovery* responder_Discovery;
      IPSME_MsgEnv*        MsgEnv;
  };
  Refs refs() const { return { _responder_Discovery.get(), _uptr_IPSME.get() };
  }
  // usage — looks almost exactly like your JS
  auto [responder_Discovery, MsgEnv] = bridge->refs();

  Option B — a tuple (no extra type):
  std::tuple<Responder_Discovery*, IPSME_MsgEnv*> refs() const {
      return { _responder_Discovery.get(), _uptr_IPSME.get() };
  }
  auto [responder_Discovery, MsgEnv] = bridge->refs();

  Key differences from your JS line to keep in mind:
  - Order, not name. auto [MsgEnv, responder_Discovery] = bridge->refs(); would
  silently swap them — the identifiers are yours to name, but they bind
  left-to-right to the struct's members in order. JS matches by key; C++ matches
  by position.
  - No subset/reorder. JS lets you grab just { MsgEnv }. Structured bindings
  must bind every member of the bundle.
  - It's a plain function call returning a value (here, cheap copies of two
  pointers) — there's no .current proxy magic; you just call refs().

  Struct (Option A) reads best because the member names document the order at
  the definition site, so a mistaken binding order is easier to catch.

  Want me to add refs() to IPSME_Bridge? If so, the existing ipsme() /
  protocol_Discovery() / eventLogPtr() accessors can stay for single-grab
  callers, and I'd just add the bundle alongside them.

❯ \btw forget the ref ... current syntax.                                       

● Got it — that .current was just the React-ref idiom, ignore it. The C++ answer
  is unchanged and simpler without it: structured bindings over a struct/tuple
  you return from the bridge.

  auto [responder_Discovery, MsgEnv] = bridge->refs();

  Still positional (matches by order, not name), and you bind the whole bundle.
  Want me to add the refs() accessor to IPSME_Bridge, or leave it with the
  single-grab ipsme() / protocol_Discovery() ones?

❯ so for this line: auto bridge= IPSME_Bridge::get_instance(uptr_app.get(),     
  _uptr_eventLog.get());                                                        
  there is no good reason to save bridge, because we can always access it again 
  via get_instance(), but getting the refs on that line would be good avoiding  
  this: g_ptr_ipsme = bridge->ipsme();                                          

● Right, and there's a subtlety worth separating out, because the two goals need
  different mechanisms:

  Killing the g_ptr_ipsme = bridge->ipsme(); line isn't actually solved by
  destructuring in main. do_read is a free function that asio calls outside
  main's scope — a local you bind in main (ref or not) is invisible to it. The
  only ways do_read can reach IPSME are a global, or the singleton. So the clean
  fix is to let do_read pull it from the singleton itself:

  // do_read, replacing g_ptr_ipsme->publish(...)
  IPSME_Bridge::get_instance()->ipsme()->publish(str_msg.c_str());

  That lets the IPSME_MsgEnv* g_ptr_ipsme global be deleted entirely — and with
  it, the assignment line you don't like.

  Not saving bridge then falls out naturally — main just initializes the
  singleton and uses it in the loop:

  IPSME_Bridge::get_instance(uptr_app.get(), _uptr_eventLog.get());   // init

  while (!gb_quit_) {
      std::this_thread::sleep_for(100ms);
      IPSME_Bridge::get_instance()->process_msgs();
  }

  So between the two ideas:
  - Destructuring refs on that line is the right tool only if main itself needs
  the handles locally — e.g. when you add the asio acceptor and main wires
  sockets. Right now main only touches process_msgs(), so it needs nothing
  local.
  - The singleton in do_read is what actually removes the global and the extra
  line.

  My recommendation: do the singleton version now (deletes the global, no saved
  bridge, no extra line), and add refs() later when main grows code that needs
  MsgEnv/responder_Discovery directly.

  Want me to apply that — delete g_ptr_ipsme, switch do_read to
  get_instance()->ipsme()->publish(...), and drop the saved bridge? I'll make
  the edits now and rebuild to confirm once your VS update finishes.

● PowerShell($msb = "C:\Program Files\Microsoft Visual
            Studio\2022\Community\MSBuild\Current\Bin\MSBuild.exe"; & $msb
            "reflector-cpp-MQTT--asio-client.vcxproj" /p:Configurat…)
  ⎿  Build succeeded.
         0 Warning(s)
         0 Error(s)
     … +2 lines (ctrl+o to expand)

● refs() is in and compiling. And yes — your last point is exactly right:
  structured bindings introduce real names into whatever scope the line sits in,
  so responder_Discovery and MsgEnv are usable right there. That part is pure
  JS-like ergonomics and works.

  But where that line can legally go is constrained by two C++ facts that decide
  this for us:

  1. Structured bindings can't be class data members. So "inside the App" can't
  mean auto [responder_Discovery, MsgEnv] as App fields — the language only
  allows structured bindings at block scope (inside a function) or namespace 
  scope (global). Inside App, it'd have to be a local in some App method, or App
  would store two plain pointer members (no destructuring).

  2. Global scope works syntactically, but constructs the bridge before main().
  This compiles and gives you global responder_Discovery / MsgEnv names:
  // namespace (global) scope
  auto [responder_Discovery, MsgEnv] =
      IPSME_Bridge::get_instance(g_app.get(), g_eventLog.get())->refs();
  …but it runs during static initialization — before main(). The bridge
  constructor subscribes to MQTT and calls announce() → publish(), and your
  main() calls mosquitto_lib_init() first thing. So global init would do MQTT
  work before mosquitto is initialized → broken/UB. You also can't split it
  (declare the names global, assign in main after lib_init) — structured-binding
  names must be bound at their declaration.

  So the realistic placements:

  - Block scope in main (recommended): one line, structured bindings, no saved
  bridge — just not "above main":
  mosquitto_lib_init();
  ...
  auto [responder_Discovery, MsgEnv] =
      IPSME_Bridge::get_instance(uptr_app.get(), _uptr_eventLog.get())->refs();
  - Free functions like do_read reach IPSME via
  IPSME_Bridge::get_instance()->ipsme() (a main local can't be seen by them
  regardless of how it's named).
  - True global names: only safe if the bridge stops doing MQTT work in its
  constructor (or it self-calls mosquitto_lib_init). That's a functional change
  to the bridge — out of bounds for "just compile."

  My read: the value you actually want — don't carry bridge around, get the refs
  in one line — is fully delivered by the block-scope-in-main version, without
  the static-init landmine. Want me to apply that (one-line structured binding
  in main, drop the saved bridge and the g_ptr_ipsme global, point do_read at
  the singleton)? Or do you specifically want the global placement, in which
  case I'll lay out what the bridge change entails first?

❯ \btw what's this reflecto.b1d4e6a2 ?                                          
  intermediate data?                                                            

● Yes — it's the project's intermediate build directory (MSVC's IntDir). Let me
  show what's in it to be concrete:

● Bash(cd "/c/Users/dev/IPSME.git/reflector-cpp-MQTT--asio-client.git"
      find reflecto.b1d4e6a2 -maxdepth 2 -type d…)
  ⎿  reflecto.b1d4e6a2
     reflecto.b1d4e6a2/x64
     reflecto.b1d4e6a2/x64/Debug
     … +20 lines (ctrl+o to expand)

● Right — it's purely intermediate build data, safe to delete (and now
  git-ignored). Per config (x64/Debug, x64/Release) it holds:

  - *.obj — one compiled object per source file
  - vc143.pdb / vc143.idb — compiler debug-symbol + incremental databases (the
  ones that hit the PDB race earlier)
  - *.ilk — incremental-linker state
  - *.tlog/, *.log, *.recipe, FileListAbsolute.txt — MSBuild's up-to-date
  tracking and bookkeeping
  - vcpkg.applocal.log — record of the DLL-copy step

  The final outputs (the .exe and copied .dlls) go to the separate x64/ dir, not
  here. Delete reflecto.b1d4e6a2/ anytime and the next build regenerates it.

  The weird name is MSVC avoiding long paths: it takes the project name
  reflector-cpp-MQTT--asio-client, truncates to 8 chars → reflecto, and appends
  an 8-hex-digit hash of the project → .b1d4e6a2. So reflecto.b1d4e6a2. It's the
  default IntDir VS picks when the project name is long, keeping intermediate
  paths well under the Windows MAX_PATH limit. (That's also why I matched it
  with reflecto.*/ in .gitignore — if the project name or hash changes, the glob
  still catches it.)

● Bash(cd /c/Users/dev/IPSME.git/reflector-cpp-MQTT--asio-client.git
      echo "=== where are the App virtuals actually CALLED? ==="…)
  ⎿  === where are the App virtuals actually CALLED? ===
     main.cpp:280:    void discover_timed_out(const DiscoverContext& ctx, c
     onst std::string& hyperport) override
     … +22 lines (ctrl+o to expand)
● Here's what the code actually shows — and it backs your instinct strongly:

  The App interface is almost entirely dead weight in this project.

  1. The three virtuals are never called. discover_timed_out,
  check_ready_installed, load_character_in_world appear only as the override
  stubs in main.cpp. Nothing in the bridge, responder, or anywhere invokes them
  — they exist purely so App can be instantiated to satisfy Interface_App's
  pure-virtual contract. They're scaffolding inherited from the tx-Decentraland
  app (install/launch a viewer), which this reflector doesn't do.
  2. The App* is used for exactly one thing: handing over a Referer.
  Responder_Discovery's constructor does _referer(kpi_App->referer()) — it
  copies the Referer once and stores its own _referer. After that, the stored
  _kpi_App pointer is never used again (the only references are commented-out
  lines 51/56).
  3. Interface_App::platforms is static — the Decentraland/SecondLife URI table.
  It needs no instance; it's reached via the class name.

  So the entire Interface_App → App machinery boils down to: deliver a Referer 
  to the bridge. That's it.

  Recommendation: drop Interface_App/App, and have
  IPSME_Bridge::get_instance(...) take a JSON::JSON_Msg::Referer directly (plus
  the IEventLog* it already takes). The static platforms table can move to a
  free constant or stay as a plain struct — it doesn't need the interface. No
  callback is even required yet, because nothing currently calls back into "the
  app."

  That leaves one question that decides the shape: what would the single 
  callback actually do? Right now nothing calls back — the bridge handles
  discovery internally, and the asio→MQTT path already goes through
  g_ptr_ipsme->publish. So before I touch anything:

  - Is the callback for the MQTT → asio direction (deliver received MQTT
  messages out to the TCP sockets — i.e. wire up the currently-orphaned
  handler_string_)?
  - Or a general "message received" hook for your own logic?
  - Or do you just want App gone and a Referer passed in, with the callback
  added later?

  Tell me which, and I'll do the minimal change — no extra scaffolding this
  time.

  - IPSME_Bridge now takes a tp_callback_string (a bool(const char*, 
  std::string) function pointer, matching the existing IPSME_MsgEnv callback
  style). get_instance(...) and the constructor thread it through.
  - handler_string calls it for any message the discovery protocol didn't
  consume:
  // not consumed by the discovery protocol: hand it back to main (MQTT -> asio)
  if (_callback_string)
      return _callback_string(msg, str_msg);
  - main registers the already-present handler_string_ (the MQTT → asio path
  that writes to the TCP sockets): get_instance(uptr_app.get(), 
  _uptr_eventLog.get(), handler_string_).

  So the bridge now calls back into main on each non-discovery MQTT message, no
  Interface_App virtuals involved. (At runtime it's a no-op until something
  populates g_set_sockets, but the wiring compiles and is in place.)

● Got it — that clarifies the split you're after. Let me play it back and not
  edit until you confirm, since you're hand-editing and I've churned enough.

  My understanding now:
  - That do_read/do_write/handler_string_ block stays in main, untouched — along
  with l4end (framing) and g_duplicate (dedup). The dedup/framing/publish logic
  lives in main.
  - The only parts that move into cpp-asio.git are the two raw asio I/O calls
  you flagged:
    - ptr_socket->async_read_some(asio::buffer(...), ...)
    - asio::async_write(*ptr_socket, asio::buffer(...), ...)

  So cpp-asio.git becomes a thin raw byte transport (owns the socket/connection,
  hides asio), roughly:
  class asio_client {
      typedef std::function<void(const char* pch, std::size_t len)>
  t_callback_read; // raw bytes -> main deframes
      void start();
      void write(std::string bytes);   // main passes already-enframed bytes -> 
  async_write
  };
  and main's do_read becomes that read callback (deframe → dedup → publish),
  while do_write/handler_string_ call asio.write(enframed).

  That's different from the asio_client I just built, which does the framing
  inside the module. If you confirm this split, I'll reshape cpp-asio.git to the
  raw-transport API above (no l4end, no dedup in the module) and leave your
  main block alone except for swapping those two asio calls.

  Two things to confirm before I touch anything:
  1. Is that raw-transport split right?
  2. That block is server-shaped — it takes a t_ptr_socket and broadcasts over a
  g_set_sockets set (multiple peers), not a single client connection. Should
  cpp-asio.git manage a set of sockets (server/reflector style), or a single
  client socket? It changes the module's API.

  Heads-up: main.cpp won't compile in its current mixed state (my earlier
  rewrite removed the asio includes / t_ptr_socket / g_set_sockets that the
  re-pasted block needs). Tell me the two answers above and I'll make it
  consistent in one pass.

● Build succeeded (0 errors). The split is now exactly the raw-transport design
  you confirmed:

  cpp-asio.git — thin byte transport (all asio hidden behind PImpl):
  - t_callback_read = void(const char* pch_data, std::size_t szt_len) → delivers
  raw bytes
  - write(std::string bytes) → sends already-framed bytes
  - owns the socket/io thread, async connect/read/write with a write queue +
  simple reconnect. No l4end, no dedup.

  main — keeps framing + dedup + publish:
  - on_asio_read(pch, len) → l4end::deframe → g_duplicate.exists →
  g_ptr_ipsme->publish (asio → MQTT)
  - handler_string_(...) → g_duplicate.cache →
  g_ptr_asio->write(l4end::enframe(str_msg)) (MQTT → asio)

  So l4end and g_duplicate stayed in main as you wanted, and only the two raw
  asio I/O calls live in the module.

  One honest caveat: I couldn't keep that pasted block byte-for-byte. It was
  written around t_ptr_socket/g_set_sockets (main holding the sockets), and once
  the socket moves into the module there's no ptr_socket to thread through or
  set to broadcast over — so do_read(t_ptr_socket)/do_write(t_ptr_socket,…)
  collapsed into the two callbacks above. The dedup/framing/publish logic and
  the log lines are preserved; the per-socket plumbing is gone. If you'd rather
  the module manage a set of sockets so that shape survives, say so and I'll
  switch it to the server/broadcast variant.

● No — l4end framing is in main, not in the asio module. That's the split you
  asked for.

  - cpp-asio.git — no l4end at all. Its .cpp doesn't include l4end-framing.h; it

  void on_asio_read(const char* pch_data, std::size_t szt_len)
  {
        l4end::deframe(&vch_buffer_, pch_data, szt_len, [](std::string str_msg)
        {
                ...
        });
  }

  It takes the raw bytes from the transport (pch_data, szt_len), runs them
  through l4end::deframe into complete messages, then dedups and publishes each.
  So the framing happens here in main, exactly as intended — the asio module
  hands over raw bytes, on_asio_read deframes them.

● Block's back and compiling (0 errors). Now, straight answers to both — and
  you're right to poke at this:

  1. "How do you catch deframe errors?" — You don't, and neither does your 
  block. Look at l4end::deframe (lines 79–145): it has no error channel. On a
  bad F00D marker, bad length, or missing DEAD it just does erase(begin()); 
  continue; — i.e. drops a byte and resyncs. On overflow it clears the buffer.
  It returns pvch_buf->size() (leftover bytes), not a status. Your block calls
  it and ignores the return too:
  l4end::deframe(&vch_buffer_, ach_recvd_, length, [](std::string str_msg){ ...
  });
  So there's nothing to catch — framing errors are swallowed/resynced inside
  deframe regardless of who calls it. My version wasn't dropping anything there.

  2. "You don't need this?" (the ec read-error block) — Yes, you absolutely do, 
  and I didn't drop it. It's in the module — asio_client.cpp, do_read:
  if (ec) {
      std::cerr << "asio_client: read ERROR! " << ec << " -- reconnecting" <<
  std::endl;
      schedule_reconnect();
      return;
  }
  The difference is what it does on error, and that's the real point you're
  driving at: your block is server-shaped — on a read error it close()s that
  socket and g_set_sockets.erase(ptr_socket) (drop one peer out of many). My
  module is client-shaped — one socket, so on error it reconnects instead. Same
  ec check, different response because the topology is different.

  So the honest summary: the ec handling is necessary and present (just
  client-style); the "deframe errors" aren't a thing either implementation
  catches because l4end doesn't expose them. Note all of this is moot in the
  current tree — we reverted to your block, and the asio_client module isn't
  wired into main at all right now. Want to leave it that way, or wire the
  module back in?

✻ Crunched for 3m 48s

※ recap: Goal: build the MQTT–asio reflector as a Visual Studio project. Your original asio block is restored in main.cpp and the whole thing compiles clean. Next: decide whether to wire the cpp-asio.git module back into main or leave the block as-is.

❯ don't touch the code right now, just answer... is there a way identify the    
  socket the read write is happening on with some kind of ID?                   

● Yes — a few ways, depending on what kind of "ID" you want:

  1. The OS socket handle — socket.native_handle()
  Returns the underlying descriptor (SOCKET on Windows, an int fd on POSIX).
  It's a small integer, unique among currently open sockets. Your old
  session::strID() even had this as a commented-out option:
  //    return std::to_string( ptr_socket_->native_handle() );
  Caveat: it's recycled by the OS after a socket closes, so it identifies a
  socket while live, not across its lifetime.

  2. The peer endpoint — socket.remote_endpoint()
  Gives the other end's address():port() — a meaningful "who am I talking to"
  ID:
  auto ep = ptr_socket->remote_endpoint();   // ep.address().to_string() + ":" +
  ep.port()
  Caveat: it throws std::system_error if the socket isn't connected (e.g. after
  an error). Use the remote_endpoint(ec) overload to avoid the throw. The full
  TCP identity is actually the 4-tuple (local endpoint + remote endpoint).

  3. The pointer itself
  In your block, t_ptr_socket is a shared_ptr<tcp::socket> and g_set_sockets is
  keyed on it — so the shared_ptr (its address) already is a unique
  per-connection handle for the process's lifetime. That's what
  g_set_sockets.erase(ptr_socket) relies on. strID() in the old code hex-printed
  ep_.data() (the sockaddr pointer) for the same purpose.

  Which to use:
  - Stable, human-readable, "which peer" → remote_endpoint() (with the ec
  overload).
  - Cheap unique token while open → native_handle().
  - In-process identity for a map/set → the shared_ptr you already hold.

  For the single-socket asio_client it's moot (one connection), but if it ever
  manages a set like your reflector block, you'd tag each connection with one of
  the above — remote_endpoint() is the usual choice for logging/identifying.

✻ Cooked for 24s

❯ my handle string printed the socket ID:     std::cerr << "handle_str_: asio[" 
  << g_set_sockets.size() << "] <- MQTT -- [" << str_msg.c_str() << "]" <<      
  std::endl;                                                                    

● That line prints g_set_sockets.size() — that's the count of sockets currently
  in the set (how many peers are connected), not a socket ID. In handler_string_
  there isn't a single socket to identify anyway: it broadcasts to all of them
  —
  for (auto it : g_set_sockets)
      do_write(it, str_msg);
  so asio[3] means "fanning this MQTT message out to 3 connected peers," not
  "socket #3."

  The places where you actually hold one specific socket are do_read and
  do_write — each gets ptr_socket. That's where a real per-socket ID would go,
  e.g. ptr_socket->native_handle() or ptr_socket->remote_endpoint(). So if you
  want the log to show which peer, the ID belongs in do_write's line (inside the
  broadcast loop), not in handler_string_ where you only know the count.

✻ Worked for 16s

❯ Does the current implementation support multiple open connections to          
  different servers?                                                            

● Short answer: no — not as multiple outbound connections to different servers.
  Two pieces, neither does it:

  The asio_client module — single connection. Its Impl holds exactly one
  tcp::socket _socket and one _ep (one address/port), and g_ptr_asio is one
  global pointer. One asio_client = one server. You'd get multi-server only by
  creating several asio_client instances (or by making the module hold a
  map<endpoint, socket> internally) plus logic to choose which one a message
  goes to.

  The g_set_sockets block — holds multiple sockets, but that's a different
  thing:
  - They're inbound/accept-style peers (the block has no connect — sockets just
  appear in the set from an acceptor elsewhere), not outbound dials to different
  servers.
  - handler_string_ broadcasts the same message to every socket in the set —
  there's no per-connection routing or per-server addressing.
  - And right now nothing even populates g_set_sockets (no acceptor/connector is
  wired in main).

  So: the set supports many peers of one role (server fan-out), the module
  supports one client connection. Neither models "connect out to server A and
  server B and route between them."

  To actually support multiple servers you'd need: a connection per server (N
  asio_clients, or a connection-manager keyed by endpoint), each tagged by an ID
  (remote_endpoint() from the earlier question), plus routing so a given
  message targets the right connection instead of broadcasting.

  One heads-up: main.cpp is currently in a half-merged state — it has two
  handler_string_ definitions and two vch_buffer_ (the module-style callbacks
  and the restored block), so it won't compile as-is. Want me to leave it for
  you, or reconcile to one of the two models?

  — publish from an io thread would race mosquitto_loop on the main thread. So

  loop (exactly as the original did with ioctx.poll()). That's the one
  deliberate difference from the client module.

● Builds clean now. To directly answer what you were looking for in main.cpp:

  Sockets are out of main — the t_ptr_socket/t_set_sockets/g_set_sockets and the
  asio includes are gone from the active code (they now live inside
  cpp-asio.git/asio_server.cpp). Your commented-out reference block is
  preserved.

  Your read callback — on_asio_read(const char* pch_data, std::size_t szt_len):
  the module hands it raw bytes, it does l4end::deframe → dedup →
  g_ptr_ipsme->publish.

  Your write — handler_string_: g_duplicate.cache(...) then
  g_ptr_asio->write(l4end::enframe(str_msg)), which broadcasts to every
  connection.

  main() now: IPSME_MsgEnv msgenv (the pulled class) +
  msgenv.subscribe(&handler_, NULL); asio_server server(kus_LISTEN_PORT, 
  on_asio_read); server.start();; loop just calls msgenv.process_msgs().

  What I did this round:
  - cpp-asio.git/asio_server.{h,cpp} (in the shared submodule, alongside
  asio_client): acceptor + per-connection socket/read-buffer/write-queue +
  broadcast, asio hidden behind PImpl. Because your pull gave the server the
  mutex-guarded class IPSME_MsgEnv, I made it threaded (own io thread,
  start()/stop(), write() posts to the io thread) — same shape as the client,
  which the single-threaded poll() model would otherwise have required.
  - Added asio_server.cpp/.h to the .vcxproj.
  - Copied g_.hpp into the server root — the pulled IPSME_MsgEnv.cpp newly
  #includes ../g_.hpp and the server project didn't have it.

  One caveat worth noting (same as the client): on_asio_read runs on the io
  thread and handler_string_ runs on the main thread, and both touch g_duplicate
  — the dedup cache isn't thread-safe, so that's a latent race if you keep the
  threaded model. The MQTT side is now safe (the mutex you pulled). Want me to
  leave it, or guard g_duplicate?

❯ What is the best solution if two projects are the same except for the         
  libraries they include.... say project X-Y and W-Z are the same except that   
  X-Y uses lib X and W-Z uses lib W (lib X and lib W having the same interface  
  allowing them to be swapped. Same for Y and Z.                                

● Great architecture question — and it's exactly the shape your codebase is
  already in (one reflector "core," swappable msgenv = MQTT/sdbus, swappable
  transport = asio-client/asio-server/ws).

  The governing principle: depend on the interface, and choose the concrete 
  implementation at build/link time — never fork the whole project per 
  combination. Forking gives you a combinatorial explosion: X-Y, X-Z, W-Y, W-Z =
  4 repos for a 2×2, and every bug fix in the common code has to be applied 4
  times.

  Concretely, ranked for your setup (MSVC + git submodules + interface headers
  like IPSME_MsgEnv.h):

  1. One shared "core" + thin per-variant shells (best fit for your submodules).
  The common code (the reflector bridge: deframe/dedup/publish, on_asio_read,
  handler_string_, main) lives once in a shared submodule/header. Each swappable
  lib sits behind a stable interface header (IPSME_MsgEnv.h, an asio_*
  transport header — you already have these). A "project" then becomes a thin
  shell: a build file + maybe a 10-line main that just #includes the core and
  links the chosen impls. X-Y and W-Z share the core submodule; they differ only
  in which impl submodules/sources they reference. This is link-time dependency
  injection.

  2. One repo, multiple build configurations.
  Keep a single project; add solution configurations (e.g. MQTT|x64, sdbus|x64)
  where each config compiles a different impl .cpp and sets a #define. CMake
  does this cleanly with an option() / cache variable (-DREFLECTOR_MSGENV=MQTT).
  No duplicated source, the build picks the combo. Good when one repo producing
  N executables is acceptable.

  3. Runtime polymorphism (abstract base + factory).
  Only if the choice must be made at runtime (e.g. config file picks transport).
  Define an abstract ITransport/IMsgEnv, implement per lib, inject via a
  factory. Flexible but adds vtables and runtime selection you don't need if the
  lib is fixed per binary.

  4. Templates / policy-based.
  Reflector<Transport, MsgEnv> instantiated as <asio_client, MQTT> vs
  <asio_server, sdbus>. Compile-time, zero-overhead, but the interfaces must be
  static and it gets gnarly to read/debug.

  For you specifically: since the lib choice is fixed per executable and you're
  already factoring each lib into its own interface-header'd submodule, option 1
  (shared core + thin shells) — or option 2 if you'd rather one repo — is the
  sweet spot. Avoid 3/4; you don't need runtime swapping or template machinery.

  The one prerequisite that makes all of this work, and which you already have:
  the swappable libs must present the identical interface (same header API), so
  the core compiles unchanged against either. That's the IPSME_MsgEnv class API
  being the same whether it's backed by MQTT or sdbus — keep that contract
  strict and the rest is just build wiring.

  Want me to sketch what the shared-core + thin-shell layout would look like for
  your reflector (which files move into the core submodule vs stay
  per-variant)?

✻ Cogitated for 1m 7s

❯ yes                                                                           

● Here's the layout. The idea: everything that's identical across variants moves
  into a shared reflector core, and each project shrinks to a ~15-line shell
  that names the two libs it wants.

  File tree

  SHARED submodules (written once):
    cpp-reflector-core.git/    reflector.hpp     ← the bridge logic
  (deframe/dedup/publish ⇄ enframe/write)
    cpp-asio.git/              asio_client.{h,cpp}, asio_server.{h,cpp}   ←
  transports, same read-cb/write API
    cpp-msgenv-MQTT.git/       IPSME_MsgEnv.{h,cpp}    ← msgenv impl A
    cpp-msgenv-sdbus.git/      IPSME_MsgEnv.{h,cpp}    ← msgenv impl B
  (identical class API)
    cpp-l4end-framing.git/     cpp-msg_cache-dedup.git/   ← shared helpers

  THIN per-variant projects (the only things that differ):
    reflector-MQTT--asio-client/   main.cpp (~15 lines)  .vcxproj
    reflector-MQTT--asio-server/   main.cpp (~15 lines)  .vcxproj
    reflector-sdbus--asio-server/  main.cpp (~15 lines)  .vcxproj
    ...

  The core (written once)

  // cpp-reflector-core.git/reflector.hpp
  #include "cpp-msg_cache-dedup.git/msg_cache-dedup.h"
  #include "cpp-l4end-framing.git/l4end-framing.h"

  // Transport = anything with .start() and .write(std::string); read bytes via 
  the cb you give it.
  // MsgEnv    = anything with .publish(const char*) and .subscribe(cb, void*).
  template <typename Transport, typename MsgEnv>
  class Reflector {
      duplicate          _dedup;
      std::vector<char>  _buf;
      Transport&         _transport;
      MsgEnv&            _msgenv;
  public:
      Reflector(Transport& t, MsgEnv& m) : _transport(t), _msgenv(m) {}

      // asio -> msgenv  (the transport's read callback points here)
      void on_read(const char* data, std::size_t len) {
          l4end::deframe(&_buf, data, len, [this](std::string msg){
              if (_dedup.exists(msg)) return;
              _msgenv.publish(msg.c_str());
          });
      }
      // msgenv -> asio
      bool on_msg(std::string msg) {
          _dedup.cache(msg, t_entry_context(30s));
          _transport.write(l4end::enframe(msg));
          return true;
      }
      void start() {
          _msgenv.subscribe(&trampoline, this);   // void* user-data carries 
  `this`
          _transport.start();
      }
  private:
      static void trampoline(const char* m, void* self) {
  static_cast<Reflector*>(self)->on_msg(m); }
  };

  The thin shells — the ONLY thing that differs per variant

  // reflector-MQTT--asio-client/main.cpp
  #include "cpp-reflector-core.git/reflector.hpp"
  #include "cpp-msgenv-MQTT.git/IPSME_MsgEnv.h"
  #include "cpp-asio.git/asio_client.h"

  int main() {
      mosquitto_lib_init();
      IPSME_MsgEnv msgenv;
      asio_client  transport;                       // ← client
      Reflector    reflector(transport, msgenv);
      transport.set_read_cb([&](const char* d, std::size_t n){
  reflector.on_read(d, n); });
      reflector.start();
      /* run loop: msgenv.process_msgs(); */
      mosquitto_lib_cleanup();
  }
  // reflector-MQTT--asio-server/main.cpp   — diff is two lines:
  #include "cpp-asio.git/asio_server.h"
      asio_server  transport(4999);                 // ← server (listens)
  Swap MQTT→sdbus the same way: change one #include and link
  cpp-msgenv-sdbus.git. The core never changes.

  What makes it work

  - Each variant = pick 2 libs, expressed as: 2 #includes + the right submodules
  in the .vcxproj. No forked logic.
  - The transport read-cb is wired in main (not the ctor) so Reflector and
  Transport can reference each other — that's the one plumbing tweak vs today
  (move the read callback from the asio_* constructor to a
  set_read_cb()/start(cb)).
  - I used a template core (zero runtime cost, no vtables) since the lib is
  fixed per binary. If you ever want to pick at runtime, swap the template for a
  common base class (ITransport/IMsgEnv) — same file layout, just virtual
  calls.
  - Adding ws-server or a 3rd msgenv later = a new thin shell, not a 4th/8th
  fork.

  The one discipline this depends on: the two IPSME_MsgEnv impls (and the two
  transports) must keep byte-identical public APIs so the core compiles against
  either unchanged.

  Want me to actually build this out — create cpp-reflector-core.git with
  reflector.hpp, move the bridge logic into it, add set_read_cb() to the
  transports, and reduce both projects' main.cpp to the thin shell? I'd do it on
  a branch so your current working tree is untouched.

❯ what I also think is shit is that it is so hard to configure the project name 
  (i.e., output name too). would be ideal if it was just a varaible. I should   
  be able to: check out, choose MsgEnv, choose transport protocol, choose

● Totally fair — .vcxproj ties the project name to the filename and bakes in a
  GUID, so "rename the project" means editing the filename, the .sln, and the
  GUID refs. That's genuinely annoying to template.

  Two separate things, though, and one is easy today:

  Output exe name is already a variable — it's TargetName, not the project name.
  You can set, in a .props (or /p: on the command line):
  <TargetName>$(ReflectorName)</TargetName>
  and ReflectorName from an env var, a props file, or msbuild 
  /p:ReflectorName=foo. So foo.exe without touching the project filename. The
  display name in Solution Explorer is the painful one — that's the filename,
  and MSBuild has no clean knob for it.

  For the whole checklist you described, the right tool is CMake — it's built
  for exactly "name + a few toggles as variables, then generate the VS project."
  Your entire workflow becomes:

  cmake_minimum_required(VERSION 3.20)

  # --- the knobs you asked for ---
  set(NAME      "reflector" CACHE STRING "project + output name")
  set(MSGENV    "MQTT"      CACHE STRING "MQTT | sdbus")
  set(TRANSPORT "asio"      CACHE STRING "asio | ws")
  set(ROLE      "server"    CACHE STRING "server | client")

  project(${NAME} CXX)

  add_executable(${NAME}
      main_${ROLE}.cpp                                   # thin shell per role
      cpp-msgenv-${MSGENV}.git/IPSME_MsgEnv.cpp          # MQTT or sdbus
      cpp-asio.git/asio_${ROLE}.cpp                      # asio_server or 
  asio_client
      cpp-l4end-framing.git/l4end-framing.cpp
      cpp-msg_cache-dedup.git/msg_cache-dedup.cpp)

  set_target_properties(${NAME} PROPERTIES OUTPUT_NAME "${NAME}")
  target_compile_features(${NAME} PRIVATE cxx_std_20)
  target_include_directories(${NAME} PRIVATE . include
      "C:/Users/dev/vcpkg.git/installed/x64-windows/include"
      "C:/Program Files/mosquitto/devel")
  target_link_directories(${NAME} PRIVATE "C:/Program Files/mosquitto/devel")
  target_link_libraries(${NAME} PRIVATE mosquitto rpcrt4)

  Then your exact checklist is:
  git clone --recursive <repo>
  cmake -B build -DNAME=my-reflector -DMSGENV=sdbus -DTRANSPORT=asio
  -DROLE=client
  cmake --build build --config Release          # -> my-reflector.exe

  - -DNAME= sets both the VS project name and the output .exe — one variable.
  - -DMSGENV, -DTRANSPORT, -DROLE pick the swappable pieces by string
  interpolation into the paths (cpp-msgenv-${MSGENV}.git, asio_${ROLE}.cpp). Add
  a new transport/msgenv → new folder, no CMake edit.
  - Want the IDE? cmake -B build -G "Visual Studio 17 2022" generates the
  .sln/.vcxproj from these variables, so you never hand-edit GUIDs again.

  You can even add a tiny configure.cmd/configure.sh that prompts for the four
  values and runs the cmake -B line, so it's literally "checkout → answer 4
  questions → compiled."

  This pairs naturally with the shared-core layout from before: the core + libs
  are submodules, and CMake is the thing that "picks 2 libs + a name" per build.

  Want me to add a CMakeLists.txt (+ a configure helper) to the reflector repo
  and verify it generates and builds one combo? I'll do it on a branch so your
  .vcxproj setup stays as the fallback.

That's genuinely annoying to template.                                                                                                            
                                                                                                                                                                         
    Two separate things, though, and one is easy today:                                                                                                                  
                                                                                                                                                                         
    Output exe name is already a variable — it's TargetName, not the project name. You can set, in a .props (or /p: on the command line):                                
    <TargetName>$(ReflectorName)</TargetName>                                                                                                                            
    and ReflectorName from an env var, a props file, or msbuild /p:ReflectorName=foo. So foo.exe without touching the project filename. The display                      
    name in Solution Explorer is the painful one — that's the filename, and MSBuild has no clean knob for it.                                                            
                                                                                                                                                                         
    For the whole checklist you described, the right tool is CMake — it's built for exactly "name + a few toggles as variables, then generate the VS                     
    project." Your entire workflow becomes:                                                                                                                              
                                                                                                                                                                         
    cmake_minimum_required(VERSION 3.20)                                                                                                                                 
                                                                                                                                                                         
    # --- the knobs you asked for ---                                                                                                                                    
    set(NAME      "reflector" CACHE STRING "project + output name")                                                                                                      
    set(MSGENV    "MQTT"      CACHE STRING "MQTT | sdbus")                                                                                                               
    set(TRANSPORT "asio"      CACHE STRING "asio | ws")                                                                                                                  
    set(ROLE      "server"    CACHE STRING "server | client")                                                                                                            
                                                                                                                                                                         
    project(${NAME} CXX)                                                                                                                                                 
                                                                                                                                                                         
    add_executable(${NAME}                                                                                                                                               
        main_${ROLE}.cpp                                   # thin shell per role                                                                                         
        cpp-msgenv-${MSGENV}.git/IPSME_MsgEnv.cpp          # MQTT or sdbus                                                                                               
        cpp-asio.git/asio_${ROLE}.cpp                      # asio_server or asio_client                                                                                  
        cpp-l4end-framing.git/l4end-framing.cpp                                                                                                                          
        cpp-msg_cache-dedup.git/msg_cache-dedup.cpp)                                                                                                                     
                                                                                                                                                                         
    set_target_properties(${NAME} PROPERTIES OUTPUT_NAME "${NAME}")                                                                                                      
    target_compile_features(${NAME} PRIVATE cxx_std_20)                                                                                                                  
    target_include_directories(${NAME} PRIVATE . include                                                                                                                 
        "C:/Users/dev/vcpkg.git/installed/x64-windows/include"                                                                                                           
        "C:/Program Files/mosquitto/devel")                                                                                                                              
    target_link_directories(${NAME} PRIVATE "C:/Program Files/mosquitto/devel")                                                                                          
    target_link_libraries(${NAME} PRIVATE mosquitto rpcrt4)                                                                                                              
                                                                                                                                                                         
    Then your exact checklist is:                                                                                                                                        
    git clone --recursive <repo>                                                                                                                                         
    cmake -B build -DNAME=my-reflector -DMSGENV=sdbus -DTRANSPORT=asio -DROLE=client                                                                                     
    cmake --build build --config Release          # -> my-reflector.exe                                                                                                  
                                                                                                                                                                         
    - -DNAME= sets both the VS project name and the output .exe — one variable.                                                                                          
    - -DMSGENV, -DTRANSPORT, -DROLE pick the swappable pieces by string interpolation into the paths (cpp-msgenv-${MSGENV}.git, asio_${ROLE}.cpp). Add                   
    a new transport/msgenv → new folder, no CMake edit.                                                                                                                  
    - Want the IDE? cmake -B build -G "Visual Studio 17 2022" generates the .sln/.vcxproj from these variables, so you never hand-edit GUIDs again.                      
                                                                                                                                                                         
    You can even add a tiny configure.cmd/configure.sh that prompts for the four values and runs the cmake -B line, so it's literally "checkout →                        
    answer 4 questions → compiled."                                                                                                                                      
                                                                                                                                                                         
    This pairs naturally with the shared-core layout from before: the core + libs are submodules, and CMake is the thing that "picks 2 libs + a name"                    
    per build. and ● Here's the layout. The idea: everything that's identical across variants moves into a shared reflector core, and each project shrinks to a ~15-line 
    shell that names the two libs it wants.                                                                                                                              
                                                                                                                                                                         
    File tree                                                                                                                                                            
                                                                                                                                                                         
    SHARED submodules (written once):                                                                                                                                    
      cpp-reflector-core.git/    reflector.hpp     ← the bridge logic (deframe/dedup/publish ⇄ enframe/write)                                                            
      cpp-asio.git/              asio_client.{h,cpp}, asio_server.{h,cpp}   ← transports, same read-cb/write API                                                         
      cpp-msgenv-MQTT.git/       IPSME_MsgEnv.{h,cpp}    ← msgenv impl A                                                                                                 
      cpp-msgenv-sdbus.git/      IPSME_MsgEnv.{h,cpp}    ← msgenv impl B (identical class API)                                                                           
      cpp-l4end-framing.git/     cpp-msg_cache-dedup.git/   ← shared helpers                                                                                             
                                                                                                                                                                         
    THIN per-variant projects (the only things that differ):                                                                                                             
      reflector-MQTT--asio-client/   main.cpp (~15 lines)  .vcxproj                                                                                                      
      reflector-MQTT--asio-server/   main.cpp (~15 lines)  .vcxproj                                                                                                      
      reflector-sdbus--asio-server/  main.cpp (~15 lines)  .vcxproj                                                                                                      
      ...                                                                                                                                                                
                                                                                                                                                                         
    The core (written once)                                                                                                                                              
                                                                                                                                                                         
    // cpp-reflector-core.git/reflector.hpp                                                                                                                              
    #include "cpp-msg_cache-dedup.git/msg_cache-dedup.h"                                                                                                                 
    #include "cpp-l4end-framing.git/l4end-framing.h"                                                                                                                     
                                                                                                                                                                         
    // Transport = anything with .start() and .write(std::string); read bytes via the cb you give it.                                                                    
    // MsgEnv    = anything with .publish(const char*) and .subscribe(cb, void*).                                                                                        
    template <typename Transport, typename MsgEnv>                                                                                                                       
    class Reflector {                                                                                                                                                    
        duplicate          _dedup;                                                                                                                                       
        std::vector<char>  _buf;                                                                                                                                         
        Transport&         _transport;                                                                                                                                   
        MsgEnv&            _msgenv;                                                                                                                                      
    public:                                                                                                                                                              
        Reflector(Transport& t, MsgEnv& m) : _transport(t), _msgenv(m) {}                                                                                                
                                                                                                                                                                         
        // asio -> msgenv  (the transport's read callback points here)                                                                                                   
        void on_read(const char* data, std::size_t len) {                                                                                                                
            l4end::deframe(&_buf, data, len, [this](std::string msg){                                                                                                    
                if (_dedup.exists(msg)) return;                                                                                                                          
                _msgenv.publish(msg.c_str());                                                                                                                            
            });                                                                                                                                                          
        }                                                                                                                                                                
        // msgenv -> asio                                                                                                                                                
        bool on_msg(std::string msg) {                                                                                                                                   
            _dedup.cache(msg, t_entry_context(30s));                                                                                                                     
            _transport.write(l4end::enframe(msg));                                                                                                                       
            return true;                                                                                                                                                 
        }                                                                                                                                                                
        void start() {                                                                                                                                                   
            _msgenv.subscribe(&trampoline, this);   // void* user-data carries `this`                                                                                    
            _transport.start();                                                                                                                                          
        }                                                                                                                                                                
    private:                                                                                                                                                             
        static void trampoline(const char* m, void* self) { static_cast<Reflector*>(self)->on_msg(m); }                                                                  
    };                                                                                                                                                                   
                                                                                                                                                                         
    The thin shells — the ONLY thing that differs per variant                                                                                                            
                                                                                                                                                                         
    // reflector-MQTT--asio-client/main.cpp                                                                                                                              
    #include "cpp-reflector-core.git/reflector.hpp"                                                                                                                      
    #include "cpp-msgenv-MQTT.git/IPSME_MsgEnv.h"                                                                                                                        
    #include "cpp-asio.git/asio_client.h"                                                                                                                                
                                                                                                                                                                         
    int main() {                                                                                                                                                         
        mosquitto_lib_init();                                                                                                                                            
        IPSME_MsgEnv msgenv;                                                                                                                                             
        asio_client  transport;                       // ← client                                                                                                        
        Reflector    reflector(transport, msgenv);                                                                                                                       
        transport.set_read_cb([&](const char* d, std::size_t n){ reflector.on_read(d, n); });                                                                            
        reflector.start();                                                                                                                                               
        /* run loop: msgenv.process_msgs(); */                                                                                                                           
        mosquitto_lib_cleanup();                                                                                                                                         
    }                                                                                                                                                                    
    // reflector-MQTT--asio-server/main.cpp   — diff is two lines:                                                                                                       
    #include "cpp-asio.git/asio_server.h"                                                                                                                                
        asio_server  transport(4999);                 // ← server (listens)                                                                                              
    Swap MQTT→sdbus the same way: change one #include and link cpp-msgenv-sdbus.git. The core never changes.                                                             
                                                                                                                                                                         
    What makes it work                                                                                                                                                   
                                                                                                                                                                         
    - Each variant = pick 2 libs, expressed as: 2 #includes + the right submodules in the .vcxproj. No forked logic.                                                     
    - The transport read-cb is wired in main (not the ctor) so Reflector and Transport can reference each other — that's the one plumbing tweak vs                       
    today (move the read callback from the asio_* constructor to a set_read_cb()/start(cb)).                                                                             
    - I used a template core (zero runtime cost, no vtables) since the lib is fixed per binary. If you ever want to pick at runtime, swap the template                   
    for a common base class (ITransport/IMsgEnv) — same file layout, just virtual calls.                                                                                 
    - Adding ws-server or a 3rd msgenv later = a new thin shell, not a 4th/8th fork.                                                                                     
                                                                                                                                                                         
    The one discipline this depends on: the two IPSME_MsgEnv impls (and the two transports) must keep byte-identical public APIs so the core compiles                    
    against either unchanged.                                                                                                                                            
                                                                                                                                                                         
    Want me to actually build this out — create cpp-reflector-core.git with reflector.hpp, move the bridge logic into it, add s in the README

● Added NSDNC to both lists (CMake knob + the README table and file tree).

  Will it work on Mac? Not as-is — but CMake is exactly the right tool to get it
  there. Three layers, and only the first is automatically portable:

  1. The CMake approach itself — yes, fully cross-platform. On Mac you'd just
  pick a different generator: cmake -B build -G Xcode (or Ninja/Unix Makefiles).
  The NAME/MSGENV/TRANSPORT/ROLE knobs work identically. That's the whole point
  of using CMake over .vcxproj.

  2. This CMakeLists.txt as written — no, it's Windows-pinned. It hardcodes:
  - MOSQUITTO "C:/Program Files/mosquitto" and VCPKG_ROOT ".../x64-windows" —
  Mac gets these from Homebrew (/opt/homebrew/...), not vcpkg-windows.
  - _WIN32_WINNT=0x0A00 and rpcrt4 — both Windows-only (rpcrt4 is the Win
  UUID/RPC lib).

  The fix is the standard CMake idiom — replace hardcoded paths with discovery:
  find_package(nlohmann_json CONFIG REQUIRED)
  find_package(jsoncons CONFIG REQUIRED)
  find_library(MOSQUITTO_LIB mosquitto)        # or pkg_check_modules(MOSQ 
  mosquitto)
  # Windows-only bits behind a guard:
  if (WIN32)
    target_compile_definitions(${NAME} PRIVATE _WIN32_WINNT=0x0A00
  _CRT_SECURE_NO_WARNINGS)
    target_link_libraries(${NAME} PRIVATE rpcrt4)
  endif()
  Then the same file configures on Win/Linux/Mac.

  3. The actual source code — this is the real work. The current main.cpp /
  g_.hpp / json_msg+ack.cpp are full of Windows-isms that won't compile under
  clang on Mac: <windows.h>, #pragma comment(lib, "wininet.lib"), <rpc.h>,
  <debugapi.h> / OutputDebugStringA, vsnprintf_s, and the MSVC #pragma 
  comment(lib, ...). Those need #ifdef _WIN32 guards or POSIX equivalents (e.g.
  UUID via libuuid/CFUUID instead of rpcrt4).

  And note the irony that makes this worth doing: NSDNC is macOS-only (it's
  NSDistributedNotificationCenter — Objective-C++, needs .mm files and
  -framework Foundation), sdbus is Linux-only, MQTT is anywhere. So "works on
  Mac" is precisely the reason to make MSGENV swappable — an NSDNC build only
  ever runs on Mac, and CMake is what lets one repo target all three.

  Want me to make the CMakeLists.txt cross-platform now (find_package +
  if(WIN32)/if(APPLE) blocks) so it's ready for the Mac/NSDNC path? I'd keep the
  Windows build working exactly as it does today.

❯ \btw "set(NAME      "reflector" " is reflector the default value? 

● Quick answer first: yes — set(NAME "reflector" CACHE STRING "...") makes
  reflector the default. CACHE means "use this value unless it's overridden," so
  -DNAME=my-thing (or an existing cache entry) wins; with no -DNAME, it falls
  back to reflector. Same for MSGENV/TRANSPORT/ROLE.

❯ \btw if I don't want to add all the -Dvariables each time, I could edit the CMakeList and just run build? 
● Windows build still good after the platform-guard restructure (reflector.exe
  produced).

  On your question — yes, but mind CMake's cache. Two clarifications that
  probably help more:

  You don't actually need -D on every build. -D is a configure-time thing. Once
  you've run cmake -B build -D... once, the values are saved in
  build/CMakeCache.txt, and after that:
  cmake --build build        # reuses the cached NAME/MSGENV/ROLE — no -D needed
  So repeated builds already need zero -D. You only re-specify when you want to
  change a value.

  Editing the set(... CACHE ...) default works, but only on a fresh configure.
  This is the catch: CACHE STRING means "use this unless already cached." So if
  build/ already exists, editing set(NAME "foo" ...) is ignored — the old cached
  value wins. To make an edited default take effect:
  ./clean.sh                 # (or just: rm -rf build)  -> clears the cache
  cmake -B build -G "..."    # fresh configure picks up the new defaults
  cmake --build build
  That's exactly why the clean command pairs with this: edit defaults → clean → 
  configure → build, no -D anywhere.

  (Don't add FORCE to the set() to dodge this — FORCE would also stop -D from
  ever overriding. The plain CACHE STRING is what keeps both paths working.)

  If you want named combos without either dance, that's what CMakePresets.json
  is for:
  { "configurePresets": [
    { "name": "client-mqtt", "generator": "Visual Studio 17 2022",
      "binaryDir": "build/client-mqtt",
      "cacheVariables": { "NAME": "reflector-client", "MSGENV": "MQTT", "ROLE":
  "client" } },
    { "name": "server-mqtt", "inherits": "client-mqtt",
      "binaryDir": "build/server-mqtt",
      "cacheVariables": { "NAME": "reflector-server", "ROLE": "server" } }
  ]}
  then just cmake --preset client-mqtt && cmake --build build/client-mqtt.

  Net: edit-defaults-and-build is fine if you clean between changes; otherwise
  -D once per build dir, or presets for named configs.

  So far this round I've added clean.sh + clean.cmd, rewritten .gitignore for
  CMake/cross-platform, and the build still works. Want me to add a short
  "Configuring & building" section to the README capturing the -D vs
  edit-defaults vs presets workflow (and drop in a starter CMakePresets.json)?

  You only touch -D again when you want to change a knob (or clean + re-edit the

● 🎉 Right on. Now "the rest" — making the knobs actually drive the build beyond
  the one combo. Here's the honest lay of the land, because there are two kinds
  of "rest":

  Easy / testable here (Windows): ROLE=server. Needs:
  1. asio_server.{h,cpp} copied into this project's cpp-asio.git (only
  asio_client is here now).
  2. The one plumbing tweak we discussed: move the read callback out of the
  transport constructor into set_read_cb(), so client and server present the
  same shape.
  3. A role-selected main — either main_${ROLE}.cpp (CMake already interpolates
  ${ROLE}) or one main.cpp keyed on a define.

  Other-platform (can't compile here): MSGENV=sdbus (Linux), MSGENV=NSDNC 
  (macOS). Those need their cpp-msgenv-*.git impls and the source ported off the
  Windows-isms — real work, but only verifiable on the target OS.

  …and one design snag to decide first. The two mains aren't actually "same
  except transport" right now:
  - the client main carries the whole IPSME bridge stack (Responder_Discovery,
  EventLog, json-msg, protocol-Discovery, the App/Interface_App), and currently
  doesn't even instantiate the transport (it's "start with no connections");
  - the server main is a plain reflector (subscribe → broadcast), no bridge.

  So before ROLE can flip between them, we need to decide: is the 
  discovery/bridge machinery part of the shared core (both client and server get
  it), or is it client-only? That answer determines whether there's one
  reflector.hpp core both shells use, or whether client and server keep
  meaningfully different mains.

  So — where do you want to start?
  - (A) Get ROLE=server building here first (copy in asio_server, set_read_cb,
  split the main) — concrete and testable today; or
  - (B) Settle the core question above (bridge = shared or client-only?) and
  extract cpp-reflector-core.git/reflector.hpp so the thin-shell model is real;
  or
  - (C) Something else you had in mind.

  My suggestion: A first (proves the server knob with the stack you already
  have), then B. But tell me which, and whether the bridge is core or
  client-only — I don't want to guess that one.

※ recap: Goal: make one CMake-configurable reflector build all variants from the four knobs. The MQTT/asio/client combo builds and runs end-to-end. Next: get ROLE=server working here by copying asio_server into cpp-asio.git, adding set_read_cb(), and splitting main per role.

❯ Ok, so how do we differentiate in main() between server and client, since     
  server needs to init this:         int i_port = kus_LISTEN_PORT;              
          asio_server server(kus_LISTEN_PORT, on_asio_read);                    
          g_ptr_asio = &server;                                                 
          server.start();                                                       

● Good question — and the answer is: don't branch at runtime; let the build 
  pick. The role is known at configure time (-DROLE=), so push the decision to
  compile-time. Two clean ways:

  Option B — one main.cpp, a compile-time #if (keeps it "in main()")

  CMake turns the ROLE string into a define:
  string(TOUPPER "${ROLE}" ROLE_UC)
  target_compile_definitions(${NAME} PRIVATE ROLE_${ROLE_UC})   # -> ROLE_SERVER
  or ROLE_CLIENT
  Then in main.cpp, typedef the transport once so the rest of main is
  role-agnostic, and branch only on the two things that genuinely differ — the
  header and the constructor:
  #if defined(ROLE_SERVER)
    #include "cpp-asio.git/asio_server.h"
    using transport_t = asio_server;
  #else
    #include "cpp-asio.git/asio_client.h"
    using transport_t = asio_client;
  #endif

  transport_t* g_ptr_asio = nullptr;   // both expose .start() and .write(), so 
  this is uniform
  ...
      // the ONLY irreducible difference: different ctor signatures
  #if defined(ROLE_SERVER)
      transport_t transport(kus_LISTEN_PORT, on_asio_read);
   // binds + accepts
  #else
      transport_t transport(kpsz_REFLECTOR_ADDRESS, kus_REFLECTOR_PORT,
  on_asio_read); // connects out
  #endif
      g_ptr_asio = &transport;
      transport.start();
  Everything else (on_asio_read, handler_string_, the loop) is identical because
  both transports share the .start() / .write() / read-callback API.

  Option A — two thin files, main_${ROLE}.cpp, CMake picks one

  Your CMake already interpolates ${ROLE} for the transport source; do the same
  for main:
  add_executable(${NAME} main_${ROLE}.cpp ...)
  main_client.cpp and main_server.cpp each construct their transport and
  #include the shared bridge logic. No preprocessor at all.

  Which to use

  - If the client and server mains are nearly identical (same bridge/dedup/loop,
  differ only in that ctor line) → Option B, one file, one tiny #if.
  - If they diverge a lot — and right now they do: the client main drags in the
  whole IPSME bridge / discovery / App stack and the server main is a plain
  reflector → Option A, two honest files, is cleaner than #if-ing out half of
  main.

  So this loops straight back to the question I flagged: is the discovery/bridge
  stack shared (both roles) or client-only? If client-only, you've effectively
  got two different mains → Option A. If you intend to extract a common
  reflector.hpp core that both roles call, the per-role file shrinks to ~12
  lines and either option is tidy.

  Want me to wire up Option B now (add the ROLE_* define to CMake + the
  transport_t typedef/#if in main.cpp), since it's the smallest step and keeps
  everything in one main()? I'll leave the bridge stack exactly as-is.

  bug the single shared buffer in main had.

  standalone server didn't have. When you're ready, that's the "bridge = shared
  or client-only?" decision — if client-only, we'd wrap that block in the #else
  too (or pull the common reflector part into the core). Want to tackle that

❯ wait, because that doesnt' fix the problem, because then EVERY IPSME

● You're right — static lib_init/lib_cleanup methods force every impl to declare
  them, even as no-ops. That's the leak, just relocated. The clean fix: each
  MsgEnv sets up its own global library automatically via a static guard in its
  .cpp, and main calls nothing. An impl with no global library (sdbus/NSDNC)
  simply omits the guard — it provides nothing. Let me redo it that way.

❯ \btw HOw about another conditional? 
● Good instinct (it'd be consistent with the ROLE conditional), but I think the
  guard is actually the better fit for this specific goal — let me lay out the
  trade-off, because the tree is mid-edit and I need to land on one.

  A conditional in main (#if defined(MSGENV_MQTT) mosquitto_lib_init();) works,
  but it puts mosquitto_lib_init() back inside main — which is the exact
  coupling you were trying to remove. main would once again "know" that MQTT
  needs mosquitto. And it doesn't scale closed: every future MsgEnv that needs
  setup means editing main to add another #if branch. main stays MsgEnv-aware,
  just conditionally.

  The static guard (in the MsgEnv's own .cpp) keeps every MsgEnv-specific detail
  inside the MsgEnv. main calls nothing and references no mosquitto. Adding
  sdbus/NSDNC never touches main — the MQTT .cpp has a guard, the others just
  don't:
  // cpp-msgenv-MQTT.git/IPSME_MsgEnv.cpp  — entirely self-contained
  namespace {
      struct lib_guard {
           lib_guard() { mosquitto_lib_init();    }
          ~lib_guard() { mosquitto_lib_cleanup(); }
      } g_lib_guard;
  }
  That's the proper encapsulation: the swappable lib owns its own lifecycle, and
  main genuinely can't tell which MsgEnv it's linked against (which is the
  whole point).

  The conditional's only edge is "explicit/visible in main, no static-init"; the
  guard's only cost is it runs at static-init (before main) — which is standard
  and safe for global lib setup (it's just WSAStartup etc.).

  My rec: the guard. I've already updated the header for it; I just need to swap
  the .cpp defs for the guard and delete the two calls from main. Want me to
  finish that — or do you specifically want the #if MSGENV_* conditional despite
  the re-coupling?

✻ Brewed for 2m 38s

❯ how does that lib guard work? how does it get called?                         

● It's a global object whose constructor and destructor are the init/cleanup —
  and the C++ runtime calls them automatically, nobody calls them explicitly.
  Here's the mechanism:

  namespace {
      struct lib_guard {
           lib_guard() { mosquitto_lib_init();    }   // ctor
          ~lib_guard() { mosquitto_lib_cleanup(); }   // dtor
      } g_lib_guard;        // <-- a variable with *static storage duration*
  }

  g_lib_guard is a namespace-scope object, so it has static storage duration
  (lives for the whole program, like a global). The runtime handles it in two
  phases:

  1. At program startup — before main() runs — the C++ runtime performs "dynamic
  initialization of static objects": it walks every such object in the program
  and runs its constructor. So lib_guard() fires → mosquitto_lib_init(). Once,
  automatically.
  2. At program shutdown — after main() returns (or exit()) — the runtime runs
  the destructors of those objects in reverse order (it's registered like an
  atexit handler). So ~lib_guard() fires → mosquitto_lib_cleanup().

  So "how does it get called?" — the startup/shutdown runtime calls it, the same
  machinery that constructs any global object. It's just RAII, with the
  "resource" being the mosquitto library and the object's lifetime being the
  program's lifetime.

  A few details that make it correct here:

  - namespace { ... } (anonymous) gives it internal linkage → it's private to
  IPSME_MsgEnv.cpp. Only the MQTT TU has one; an sdbus/NSDNC .cpp simply has
  none. No name clash, no shared symbol.
  - It actually runs because IPSME_MsgEnv.cpp is compiled into the binary and
  its methods (publish, subscribe, …) are used — so the translation unit is
  linked in, and its static object comes along. (Worth knowing: if a static
  guard sat in a TU that a static library pulled in but nothing referenced, the
  linker could drop it. Not our case — we compile the .cpp straight into the
  exe.)
  - Ordering is safe: the only risk with pre-main init is the "static init order
  fiasco" — depending on another global that isn't constructed yet. lib_guard
  depends on nothing, and nothing touches mosquitto before main (the
  IPSME_MsgEnv instances are created at runtime inside main, long after all
  static init finishes). So "init before first use" is guaranteed.

  Net: it's exactly the mosquitto_lib_init()/cleanup() calls you had in main,
  but moved into the MsgEnv and triggered by object lifetime instead of by hand
  — so main doesn't call anything and stays MsgEnv-agnostic.

  Want me to finish wiring it (swap the .cpp defs for this guard, delete the two
  calls in main) and build?
